This is a digital copy of a book that was preserved for generations on library shelves before it was carefully scanned by Google as part of a project 
to make the world’s books discoverable online. 

It has survived long enough for the copyright to expire and the book to enter the public domain. A public domain book is one that was never subject 
to copyright or whose legal copyright term has expired. Whether a book is in the public domain may vary country to country. Public domain books 
are our gateways to the past, representing a wealth of history, culture and knowledge that’s often difficult to discover. 


Marks, notations and other marginalia present in the original volume will appear in this file - a reminder of this book’s long journey from the 
publisher to a library and finally to you. 


Usage guidelines 
Google is proud to partner with libraries to digitize public domain materials and make them widely accessible. Public domain books belong to the 


public and we are merely their custodians. Nevertheless, this work is expensive, so in order to keep providing this resource, we have taken steps to 
prevent abuse by commercial parties, including placing technical restrictions on automated querying. 


We also ask that you: 


+ Make non-commercial use of the files We designed Google Book Search for use by individual 
personal, non-commercial purposes. 


and we request that you use these files for 


+ Refrain from automated querying Do not send automated queries of any sort to Google’s system: If you are conducting research on machine 
translation, optical character recognition or other areas where access to a large amount of text is helpful, please contact us. We encourage the 
use of public domain materials for these purposes and may be able to help. 


+ Maintain attribution The Google “watermark” you see on each file is essential for informing people about this project and helping them find 
additional materials through Google Book Search. Please do not remove it. 


+ Keep it legal Whatever your use, remember that you are responsible for ensuring that what you are doing is legal. Do not assume that just 
because we believe a book is in the public domain for users in the United States, that the work is also in the public domain for users in other 
countries. Whether a book is still in copyright varies from country to country, and we can’t offer guidance on whether any specific use of 
any specific book is allowed. Please do not assume that a book’s appearance in Google Book Search means it can be used in any manner 
anywhere in the world. Copyright infringement liability can be quite severe.

PREFACE. 


The Parish of Eglingham is divided into sixteen Townships, 
viz. : Bassington, Beanley, Brandon, Branton, Crawley, Ditch- 
burn (East and West), Eglingham, Harehope, Hedgeley, East 
Lilburn, West Lilburn, New Bewick, Old Bewick, Shipley, 
Titlington, and Wooperton, which it has not been thought advis- 
able to include in the Index Locorum owing to their frequent 
occurrence in the Registers. 


No traces of any pre-conquest building have been found, 
but as Eglingham formed a part of the possessions granted to 
the Church of Lindisfarne by King Ceolwulph, it is in every way 
probable that a Church existed in Saxon times. At the west end 
of the present Church, which is dedicated to St. Maurice, there 
is a fine border tower, but the great bulk of the existing 
structure is of late workmanship. 


Previous to the Reformation there were four Chapels 
dependent on the Church of Eglingham. They were situated at 
Old Bewick, West Lilburn, Brandon, and Wooperton; each 
had a graveyard attached to it. The Norman Chapel of Old 
Bewick was repaired in 1867, and services are regularly held 
there; at West Lilburn interments occasionally take place, and 
there are some interesting fragments of masonry; at Brandon 
nothing remains except the graveyard, which has been disused 
since 1820; at Wooperton the site of the Chapel-yard, which 
comprises three roods, had been ploughed out, but was reclaimed 
by a former Vicar. 


Since the year 1843 the Vicarage of Eglingham has been 
annexed to the Archdeaconry of Lindisfarne. 


The Registers of Baptisms and Burials date from 1662; 
those of marriages from 1663. 


iv. 
The Banns Book of Eglingham commencing in 1754 has 
been compared with the Marriage Registers. Entries relating 


to people whose Banns were called at Eglingham Church, but 
who were not married there, are given on pages 104-109. 


Where the entry is illegible, or where there is no entry at 
all, I have indicated it by [d/ank], and where any doubt as to the 
name existed, by a query. 


The letters Egl. stand for Eglingham ; the letters dc. in 
the Marriage Registers indicate that the Marriage was solem- 
nized by License: where this does not occur it was in all cases 
performed after the Publication of Banns. 


It is well to remind readers that previous to 1752 the year 
began on the 25th of March, instead of, as now, on the ist of 
January. 

K. A. M. 
Eglingham Vicarage, August 1899.

This Volume measures 14 x 10 in. and is 1 in. thick. It is of 
parchment and bound in leather. The leaves containing the 
different entries are very much intermixed ; many have probably 
been lost, and the book has been re-bound at a comparatively 
recent date. The Volume contains 152 pages all inscribed. 


B. Baptisms from 1765 to 1809. 
BurIiA_s from 1773 to 1809. 


This Volume, of parchment, and leather-bound, measures 
12% x 8 in. and is % in. thick. It contains 84 pages, of which 
66 are inscribed. 


C. Baptisms from 1798 to 1819. 
Buriats from 1798 to 1819. 


This Volume is of paper and bound in leather. It measures 
55% 10% in. and is 1 in. thick. 


The above Registers close the joint Register Books.

BANNS. 


The following Entries, commencing 1754, are Banns of those 
people whose Banns were called at Eglingham Church, but 
were not married there. 


‘‘ Egil.” after a name stands for Eglingham. 


The last date of publication is given. After 1778 the date 
of delivery of Certificate is given. 


1754- 
George Edington, Brankston, and Sarah Wilkinson, Eg!., May 26. 
William Henderson, Eg!., and Ann Ratster, Whittingham, May 26. 
William Ellet, Egl., and Ann Bard, Whittingham, May 26.

ton, May 16.

NOTES IN MARRIAGE REGISTER. | 


1780. 

Mem.—That on the 23rd dayof Nov., 1780, Robt. Ogle, Esqr., 
of Eglingham in this parish, and Miss Hannah Compton, of 
Gainslaw, in ye par. of Berwick upon Tweed, were married in 
ye Parish Church of Berwick aforesaid by the Revd. Mr. Romney, 
Vicar. 

1781. 


Mem.—That George Brown and Elizabeth Richardson, both 
of this Par., were married at Mordington in Scotland, on ye 16th 
of October, 1781, as appears to me by Cert. for that purpose 
under ye hand of ye Revd. James Smith, minister of that Par. 
H. Hodgson. 

1785. 

Mem.—Thomas Armstrong, of Ingram Par., and Eleanor 
Crisp came to be married here on ye 17th June, but not having 
a Certificate in Ingram, where they had omitted to give in their 
names for Publication, the marriage was not solemnized here, 
but a Certificate granted in order to their marriage in Scotland, 
where they were ‘‘ lawfully married” on ye 18th day of June, 
1785, aS appears by a Cert. from James Smith, Min*:. of 
Mordington. 

1800. 


Mem.—That on Friday, ye 23rd day of May, 1800, Henry 
Collingwood, Esqr., of Lilburn Tower in this Par., was married 
in Rothbury Church to Miss Mary Anne Watson, second daughter 
of ye Revd. Dr. Watson, Rector of that Parish. H. Hodgson. 


1801. 


Mem.—That John Carr, Esqr., of West Ditchburn in this 
Par., and Miss [d/ank] Taylor, daughter of ye late [2/an] of 
Wear™., in ye County of Durham, were married at Monkwearmo. 
aforesaid on Tuesday, ye 10th day of March last, as was properly 
certified to me on ye occasion. H. Hodgson. 


1804. 
Mem.—That Mr. Nicholas Burrell, of Bassington in this 
Par., and Mary, one of ye daughters of ye late Mr. Alex. Veitch, 
of ye City of Glasgow, were married in Edinburgh on ye 25th 


day of Dec., 1804, as is certified to us by ye Revd. H. Moncrieff 
Wellwood, Min**: of St. Cuthbert’s, Edin. Hugh Hodgson, Vicar.
